<div id="review_2389748142" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2389748142" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40275186-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494083045p2/40275186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2389748142?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/40275186-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40275186-sarah?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40275186-sarah?shelf=translated">translated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2389748142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7759108627104721622">I have to say- I'm super disappointed to be writing another 3 star review for this series and also relieved that it's over. I originally attributed my feelings about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23168817.The_Dark_Forest__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past___2_' title='The Dark Forest (Remembrance of Earth’s Past, #2) by Liu Cixin' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dark Forest</a> being sort of mediocre to the translator, and while I stand by the conclusion that Ken Liu did it better, I don't think it's entirely Maritnsen's fault. <br/><br/>I don't know if I wish I'd stopped after <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518872.The_Three_Body_Problem__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past__1_' title='The Three-Body Problem (Remembrance of Earth’s Past #1) by Liu Cixin' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Three-Body Problem</a>. It was certainly a lot of time to devote to a trilogy that I felt meh about, but I think I was too i</span>
  <span id="freeText7759108627104721622" style="display:none">I have to say- I'm super disappointed to be writing another 3 star review for this series and also relieved that it's over. I originally attributed my feelings about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23168817.The_Dark_Forest__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past___2_" title="The Dark Forest (Remembrance of Earth’s Past, #2) by Liu Cixin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Forest</a> being sort of mediocre to the translator, and while I stand by the conclusion that Ken Liu did it better, I don't think it's entirely Maritnsen's fault. <br /><br />I don't know if I wish I'd stopped after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518872.The_Three_Body_Problem__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past__1_" title="The Three-Body Problem (Remembrance of Earth’s Past #1) by Liu Cixin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Three-Body Problem</a>. It was certainly a lot of time to devote to a trilogy that I felt meh about, but I think I was too intrigued not to know how it all ended. When I think about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518872.The_Three_Body_Problem__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past__1_" title="The Three-Body Problem (Remembrance of Earth’s Past #1) by Liu Cixin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Three-Body Problem</a>, I recall the humorous one liners that broke up the tension, I recall the mystery and the intrigue surrounding the Trisolarans, the suspense, the weirdness of it all.<br /><br />Where did all that go for books two and three? Who felt either of those books warranted an additional 200/300 pages over the first? For a series that spans 1400+ pages, I could probably sum books 2 and 3 up with one line each. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25451264.Death_s_End__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past__3_" title="Death's End (Remembrance of Earth’s Past #3) by Liu Cixin" rel="nofollow noopener">Death's End</a> gives us a female protagonist, that I'm sad to say is insanely stereotypical. Cheng Xin is pretty. Cheng Xin is soft. Cheng Xin has maternal instincts. She's feminine and flowery and though she's described as smart she fails in every task she's given and the readers are led to believe that "men's jobs" should be left to the men. I know Liu can do better. He gave us Ye Wenjie after all, who was none of those things, but also brings up another point, that the apocalypse was initiated by a woman, and major spoilers: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ultimately allowed to happen because of another woman. Only Luo Ji could have stopped it. Only Thomas Wade. Cheng Xin finds some small redemption in giving up Universe 647, but at that point, did it really matter? Was she <i>really</i> redeemed? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />But my biggest complaint about this book is most definitely the conclusion. The first half of the book, I actually did enjoy quite a bit. The last half was dragged out unnecessarily, nothing is accomplished the plot really seems to go nowhere. I could have lived with all this if the conclusion had paid off, but it didn't. <br /><br />End of Series spoilers ahead: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[After all that, after Cheng Xin and AA escape, after we learn that Blue Space and Gravity made it to several inhabitable worlds, we never get to see those worlds. We never get to see what became of the remainder of humanity. We never learn anything more about Singer, who cleanses systems or why. We're given a frustratingly short glimpse into the thoughts of an enemy greater than Trisolaris and then nothing else ever comes of it. And then to top it off, Cheng Xin and Yun Tianming never even get their space rendezvous? <br /><br />On the one hand, the conclusion is sort of happy. A small population of humanity survived to find and inhabit other worlds. They were not exterminated (at least not for millions of years). Cheng Xin's ending and existence isn't ever happy and her personal conclusion was a huge disappointment. This book is frustratingly dark, and without the humor to break it up, I really believe it needed some kind of happy ending for the protagonist. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I will say that the story is grand. It spans literally millions of years, galaxies, etc. The overall feeling is that this is humanity's story and not one particular character's. It draws some interesting conclusions, and certainly some relevant ideas about human nature. These are books where the individual stories are sacrificed in favor of the bigger picture, so if that's what draws you in as a reader, you will probably get more enjoyment out of these books than I did. If you're reading hoping to recapture some of the elements of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518872.The_Three_Body_Problem__Remembrance_of_Earth_s_Past__1_" title="The Three-Body Problem (Remembrance of Earth’s Past #1) by Liu Cixin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Three-Body Problem</a> I think you can safely stop reading there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7759108627104721622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2980870080" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2980870080" />
    <a title="ChopinFC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc"><img alt="ChopinFC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545283749p2/51633786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2980870080?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ChopinFC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ChopinFC" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc">ChopinFC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2980870080" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4466225693422180667"><b>5 Stars (Masterclass)<br/><br/>Stunning in conception, originality and execution!</b><br/><br/>I believe Cixin Liu's <i>Death's End</i> is his magnum opus, a perfect end to a fantastic, at times disturbing but always incredibly original series! <u>Everything is amplified in <i>Death's End</i></u>. Nothing is left for posterity, as Liu dwells deep into the human psyche, the survival of the human species and space exploration. <br/><br/><b> The Sci-fi concepts on <i>Death's End</i>are incredible, and often left me in awe of his creativity and mastery of the sub</b></span>
  <span id="freeText4466225693422180667" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars (Masterclass)<br /><br />Stunning in conception, originality and execution!</b><br /><br />I believe Cixin Liu's <i>Death's End</i> is his magnum opus, a perfect end to a fantastic, at times disturbing but always incredibly original series! <u>Everything is amplified in <i>Death's End</i></u>. Nothing is left for posterity, as Liu dwells deep into the human psyche, the survival of the human species and space exploration. <br /><br /><b> The Sci-fi concepts on <i>Death's End</i>are incredible, and often left me in awe of his creativity and mastery of the subject!!!</b><br /><br /><i>Death's End</i> achievement is quite breathtaking, and its scope boundless! Liu's Remembrance of Earth’s Past trilogy spans hundreds of years (technically speaking, millions). It interconnects at least four interstellar civilizations, as well as dozens of important characters. In <i>Death's End</i>, we return immediately after the events of the second installement. Earth and Trisolarans have achieved mutual peace agreements, and soon the exchange of cultural/technology information starts to flow between both species. <br /><br /><b> Nothing is as it seems in <i>Death's End</i>. Assume nothing, expect the worst outcomes for the survival of the human race.</b> That is certainly a driving motif in Liu's conception. The 'Dark Forest' ( explained in previous books), is never so apparent than in this last epic installment. It's no longer enough for humans to think "are we alone in the universe?"; on the contrary survival only comes with " we are not alone, and we need 'dark forest' deterrence to prevent the annihilation of the human race"!!<br /><br /><br />Liu's imagination has no boundaries. I really connected with the protagonist, 'Cheng Xin'- as she traverses centuries ( and even more), in her quest to ensure human viability. There are broad philosophical concepts in the novel, but they never feel too forced or disconnected from the narrative. The Sci-fi elements are brilliantly told, and the breath of knowledge Liu incorporates in the novel, go along away at making it all seem 'realistic'! That in essence is the scariest shit about the entire series:<br /><br /><u>
  <b> Liu's masterfully makes the point that the human race and our world will never be safe from other trans-galactic, more intelligent and ominous species!!</b>
</u><br /><br /><br /><br /><b>It's no surprise Cixin Liu's Remembrance of Earth's Past trilogy, won the Hugo Award for Best Novel in 2015. His concluding novel <i>Death's End</i> is nothing short of Sci-fi masterpiece, that left me in awe of its concepts and execution. Bravo Liu!!<br /><br />5 S.T.A.R.S!!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4466225693422180667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3393860112696114475">Book 1: 4*<br/>Book 2: 4.5*<br/>Book 3: 5<br/><br/>Perhaps the great compliment I can give a series is: I bet it will be even better on re-read. <br/><br/>I don't re-read often. Even series I loved don't get a re-read because often they're simple and fun. This was complexed and thought provoking. You don't causally read a series such as this. If you do you miss key bits of information and end up lost. <br/><br/>Truly epic in scale and outcome and yet open ended and open to interpretation. Stories within stories where the author never </span>
  <span id="freeText3393860112696114475" style="display:none">Book 1: 4*<br />Book 2: 4.5*<br />Book 3: 5<br /><br />Perhaps the great compliment I can give a series is: I bet it will be even better on re-read. <br /><br />I don't re-read often. Even series I loved don't get a re-read because often they're simple and fun. This was complexed and thought provoking. You don't causally read a series such as this. If you do you miss key bits of information and end up lost. <br /><br />Truly epic in scale and outcome and yet open ended and open to interpretation. Stories within stories where the author never once heads in the direction you think and yet where implications from book one are still playing out at the end. <br /><br />Truly a masterpiece. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N7z3FBy4xf7+EeyxuHrRl0zfZN+uxlcltVGqgvuoU7c3iXHJ0b/6UhqxXDns0L31UzJM9BGyAKOoPpU8lEGiSg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WehOYWQD886665aWOasW1THokFA1bTgMWn6ByQwYT1JZ3ci8qQTMYl5LJh5tAXq3LgW4e4oZb4pHEb53Y/G+rw==')})
  }
